[5:0:66,164] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[5:1:66,183] 2790 - COASTAL CONSERVANCY PROGRAM  

[5:2:66,200] The Coastal Conservancy seeks to achieve the following goals:  

[6:0:65,218] • Protect and enhance habitats, wetlands, scenic open space, working lands and urban waterfronts along the California coast  

[6:1:76,227] and around San Francisco Bay.  

[7:0:65,243] • Increase public access to the coast and outdoor recreational opportunities by creating new parks, trails and recreational  

[7:1:76,253] amenities.  

[8:0:65,269] • Prepare for and reduce the unavoidable impacts of climate change on the coastal region and San Francisco Bay Area.  

[8:1:65,284] • Support education projects and programs related to the preservation, enhancement, and enjoyment of coastal resources.  

[8:2:65,300] • Facilitate improvement of existing, and the development of new, lower cost accommodations within one and one-half miles of  

[8:3:76,310] the coast.  

[9:0:66,327] 2805 - STATE COASTAL CONSERVANCY LOCAL ASSISTANCE PROGRAM  

[10:0:66,347] The State Coastal Conservancy provides grants and technical assistance to local governments, nonprofits and other project  

[10:1:66,357] partners for the acquisition of land and easements, the development of public facilities, and the restoration of habitat. The State  

[10:2:66,366] Coastal Conservancy helps to implement the State's federally approved Coastal Management Program and supports programs  

[10:3:66,376] that increase public access to the coast. The Conservancy has participated in the protection of more than 390,000 acres of  

[10:4:66,386] coastal lands through acquisition of fee title and conservation easements. The Conservancy has helped restore more than  

[10:5:66,396] 33,000 acres of habitat.  

[11:0:66,415] Through its projects, the Conservancy has established approximately 160 new coastal accessways and built more than 168  

[11:1:66,425] miles of new trails.  

[12:0:66,442] State Coastal Conservancy funds are primarily expended for purposes of local assistance but may also be expended for capital  

[12:1:66,452] outlay purposes, see Program 2820.  

[12:2:66,469] 2820 - STATE COASTAL CONSERVANCY CAPITAL OUTLAY PROGRAM  

[12:3:66,487] The State Coastal Conservancy provides grants and technical assistance to state agencies for the acquisition of land and  

[12:4:66,496] easements, the development of public facilities, and the restoration of habitat. The State Coastal Conservancy helps to  

[12:5:66,506] implement the State's federally approved Coastal Management Program. The Conservancy has participated in the protection of  

[12:6:66,516] more than 390,000 acres of coastal lands through acquisition of fee title and conservation easements and the Conservancy has  

[12:7:66,526] helped restore more than 33,000 acres of habitat.

[7:0:183,263] 3790   Department of Parks and Recreation  

[8:0:66,284] The mission of the California Department of Parks and Recreation (Parks) is to provide for the health, inspiration, and  

[9:0:66,294] education of the people of California by helping to preserve the state's extraordinary biological diversity, protecting its most  

[9:1:66,304] valued natural, cultural and historical resources, and creating opportunities for high-quality outdoor recreation for current and  

[9:2:66,313] future generations to enjoy. With increased urbanization, the establishment of park units and recreation areas accessible to the  

[9:3:66,323] major population centers of the state has become particularly important. Specific activities include: stewardship of natural  

[9:4:66,333] resources, historic, cultural and archeological sites, and artifacts and structures; provision of interpretive services for park  

[9:5:66,343] visitors; construction and maintenance of campsites, trails, visitor centers, museums, and infrastructure such as roads and  

[9:6:66,352] water systems; and creation of recreational opportunities such as hiking, bicycling, fishing, swimming, horseback riding,  

[9:7:66,362] jogging, camping, picnicking, and off-highway vehicle recreation. In addition, the Division of Boating and Waterways funds,  

[9:8:66,372] plans, and develops boating facilities on waterways throughout California and ensures safe boating for the public by providing  

[9:9:66,382] financial aid and training to local law enforcement agencies.  

[10:0:66,401] Because Parks' programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, Parks has a capital outlay program to support this need.  

[10:1:66,411] For the specifics on Parks' capital outlay program see "Infrastructure Overview."

[2:0:142,32] 3810   Santa Monica Mountains Conservancy - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] The Santa Monica Mountains Conservancy acquires, restores, and consolidates lands in the Santa Monica Mountains, Rim of  

[3:1:66,78] the Valley Trail Corridor, Upper Los Angeles River Watershed, and watersheds of Santa Monica Bay for park, recreation, and  

[3:2:66,88] conservation purposes. The Conservancy may:  

[3:3:65,105] • Lease, rent, sell, transfer, or exchange lands for park purposes.  

[4:0:65,121] • Award grants or interest free loans to state and local agencies to purchase or restore park, recreation, conservation, or  

[4:1:76,131] buffer-zone areas to ensure that the character and intensity of development on these lands is generally compatible with and  

[4:2:76,141] does not adversely impact the environment.  

[5:0:65,156] • Implement programs to improve access from the inner city areas surrounding the Conservancy, thereby providing  

[5:1:76,166] recreational opportunities for all residents.  

[5:2:65,182] • Manage the Rim of the Valley Trail Corridor recreational trail.  

[6:0:65,198] • Plans for restoration, recreation, and conservation projects for the Los Angeles River and Upper Los Angeles River  

[6:1:76,207] Watershed.

[6:0:104,199] 3820   San Francisco Bay Conservation and Development Commission  

[7:0:66,220] The San Francisco Bay Conservation and Development Commission is a state planning and regulatory agency with regional  

[7:1:66,230] authority. Its mission is to protect and enhance the   San Francisco Bay, and to encourage the Bay's responsible and productive  

[7:2:66,240] use. The Commission authored and maintains the San Francisco Bay Plan, and relies on the McAteer-Petris Act and other  

[7:3:66,250] statutory and regulatory authorities to maximize public access to the Bay and minimize Bay fill. The Commission issues permits  

[7:4:66,259] for filling, dredging, and development projects within the Bay, along the Bay shoreline, and within salt ponds and certain  

[7:5:66,269] managed wetlands adjacent to the Bay. The Commission also implements the Suisun Marsh Preservation Act of 1977. By  

[7:6:66,279] statute, the Commission develops and implements the federal Coastal Zone Management Act's program for the Bay and  

[7:7:66,289] exercises authority over federal activities otherwise not subject to state control. The Commission leads the ongoing multi-

[7:8:66,299] agency regional effort to address the impacts of rising sea level and climate change on the Bay and along the shoreline.

[12:0:81,613] 3825   San Gabriel and Lower Los Angeles Rivers and Mountains Conservancy  

[13:0:66,634] The San Gabriel and Lower Los Angeles Rivers and Mountains Conservancy was established in 1999 to acquire and manage  

[13:1:66,644] public lands. Through these acquisitions, the Conservancy provides for additional open space, low-impact recreational uses,  

[13:2:66,654] educational uses, water conservation and watershed improvement, and wildlife and habitat restoration and protection. These  

[13:3:66,664] acquisitions also help to preserve the San Gabriel Mountains and the San Gabriel and Lower Los Angeles Rivers and their  

[13:4:66,673] tributaries, consistent with existing and adopted river and flood control projects for the protection of life and property.

[11:0:195,519] 3830   San Joaquin River Conservancy  

[12:0:66,540] The mission of the San Joaquin River Conservancy is to acquire, preserve, manage, and promote access to lands within the  

[12:1:66,550] flood plain on both sides of the San Joaquin River from Friant Dam to Highway 99.  

[12:2:66,567] Specific activities are to:  

[13:0:65,584] • Implement the San Joaquin River Parkway Master Plan, a 22-mile regional greenspace and wildlife corridor along both sides  

[13:1:76,594] of the river extending from Friant Dam to Highway 99, with an interconnected trail system and recreational and educational  

[13:2:76,604] features.  

[14:0:65,620] • Operate and manage lands for public access, recreation, and enjoyment consistent with the protection of natural and cultural  

[14:1:76,629] resources.  

[15:0:65,645] • Protect, enhance, and restore riparian and riverine habitat and ecological diversity.  

[15:1:65,661] • Provide for multi-benefit water quality, water supply, ecosystem and watershed protection and restoration.  

[15:2:65,677] • Facilitate the development of the parkway by assisting other entities in conserving and improving their lands within the  

[15:3:76,687] parkway, and to garner public support to secure its future.  

[15:4:65,702] • Acquire land from willing sellers to facilitate the above activities with a target of 5,900 acres.  

[16:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

[5:0:210,208] 3835   Baldwin Hills Conservancy  

[5:1:66,229] The Baldwin Hills Conservancy was established in 2000 to acquire open space and manage public lands within the Baldwin  

[5:2:66,239] Hills area and to provide recreation, restoration, and protection of wildlife habitat for the public's enjoyment and educational  

[5:3:66,249] experience.  

[5:4:66,268] Specific agency responsibilities are to:  

[5:5:65,286] • Approve the Baldwin Hills Park Master Plan.  

[6:0:65,302] • Undertake site improvement projects, regulate public access, construct new facilities as needed for outdoor recreation, and  

[6:1:76,311] provide for the appreciation and protection of natural resources.  

[6:2:65,327] • Prioritize and implement acquisition of additional recreational and open space land within the Baldwin Hills area.  

[6:3:65,343] • Provide recreational, open space, wildlife habitat restoration and protection of lands for educational use within the area.  

[6:4:65,359] • Conduct the necessary planning activities for the area.  

[7:0:65,374] • Approve conservancy funded projects that advance the policies and priorities set forth by the enabling statute.  

[7:1:65,390] • Develop and coordinate a program of resource stewardship for optimum recreational and natural resource value based on  

[7:2:76,400] the needs of the surrounding community.  

[8:0:65,416] • Provide for the public's enjoyment, and enhance recreational and educational experiences on public lands in a manner  

[8:1:76,425] consistent with the protection of lands and resources in the area.

[6:0:203,235] 3840   Delta Protection Commission  

[7:0:66,256] The mission of the Delta Protection Commission is to protect, maintain, enhance, and enrich the overall quality of the Delta  

[7:1:66,266] environment and economy, with a focus on agriculture, recreation, and natural resources,   while remaining   mindful of the  

[7:2:66,276] importance of the Delta to all Californians. The Commission   supports orderly, balanced conservation and development of Delta  

[7:3:66,286] land resources and provides a forum for Delta residents to engage in decisions regarding actions to recognize and enhance the  

[7:4:66,295] unique cultural, recreational, and agricultural resources of the Delta. The Commission identifies and makes recommendations  

[7:5:66,305] on methods of preserving the Delta as an evolving place and promotes Delta legacy communities, regional economic  

[7:6:66,315] sustainability, and emergency response preparedness.

[10:0:202,459] 3845   San Diego River Conservancy  

[11:0:66,480] The mission of the San Diego River Conservancy is to implement the San Diego River Conservancy Act through programs  

[11:1:66,490] emphasizing Land Conservation, Recreation and Education, Natural and Cultural Resources, Water Quality and Natural Flood  

[11:2:66,499] Conveyance, Organizational Capacity, and the San Diego Rivers Watershed Consortium. This Conservancy’s mission will be  

[11:3:66,509] accomplished in part by building with our partners the San Diego River Trail stretching over 52 miles from the headwaters in  

[11:4:66,519] Julian to the Pacific Ocean. The Conservancy has established advisory panels to assist in restoring and enhancing three  

[11:5:66,529] nearby watersheds: the Otay River, Sweetwater River, and Tijuana River. Working with stakeholders within these watersheds  

[11:6:66,538] fosters collaboration among governments, public agencies and nonprofit organizations, and leverages grant funding to achieve  

[11:7:66,548] an array of conservation objectives for the region with an emphasis on native habitat restoration and mitigating the impacts of  

[11:8:66,558] climate change, seawater intrusion in local watersheds, sea level rise, and the risk of wildfire and flooding.

[6:0:66,397] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[6:1:66,416] 3220 - SIERRA NEVADA CONSERVANCY PROGRAM  

[7:0:66,435] Established pursuant to Chapter 726, Statutes of 2004, the Conservancy is authorized to:  

[7:1:65,452] • Provide increased opportunities for tourism and recreation.  

[8:0:65,468] • Protect, conserve, and restore the region's physical, cultural, archaeological, historical, and living resources.  

[8:1:65,484] • Aid in the preservation of working landscapes.  

[8:2:65,500] • Reduce the risk of natural disasters, such as wildfires.  

[8:3:65,516] • Protect and improve water and air quality.  

[9:0:65,531] • Assist the regional economy through the operation of the Conservancy's program.  

[9:1:65,547] • Undertake efforts to enhance public use and enjoyment of lands owned by the public.  

[10:0:66,564] In support of these programs, the Conservancy facilitates collaborative planning efforts with local and regional governments,  

[10:1:66,574] community groups and interested parties, provides technical assistance, and initiates and funds projects to identify and fill  

[10:2:66,584] critical needs in the Sierra Nevada region.

[5:0:196,202] 3860   Department of Water Resources  

[6:0:66,223] The Department of Water Resources protects, conserves, develops, and manages California's water supply. The Department  

[6:1:66,232] evaluates existing water resources, forecasts future water needs, and explores potential solutions to meet the state’s growing  

[6:2:66,242] needs for personal use, irrigation, industry, recreation, power generation, and fish and wildlife. The Department also works to  

[7:0:66,252] prevent and minimize flood damage, oversee the safety of dams, and educate the public about the importance of water and its  

[7:1:66,262] efficient use.  

[8:0:66,281] Because the Department's programs drive a need for infrastructure investment, the Department has a capital outlay program to

[15:0:66,495] PROGRAM DESCRIPTIONS  

[16:0:66,514] 3230 - CONTINUING FORMULATION OF THE CALIFORNIA WATER PLAN  

[17:0:66,532] The California Water Plan is the state's strategic plan for the efficient use, management and development of the state's water  

[17:1:66,541] resources. The Plan is updated every five years and provides a framework for water managers, legislators, and the public to  

[17:2:66,551] consider options and make decisions regarding California's water future. The Plan evaluates current and future water  

[17:3:66,561] conditions, challenges and opportunities. It presents basic data and information on California's water resources including water  

[17:4:66,571] supply evaluations and assessments of existing and future agricultural, urban, and environmental water uses. The Plan  

[17:5:66,580] identifies and evaluates multiple future scenarios and over 30 resource management strategies such as conservation,  

[17:6:66,590] recycling, desalination, transfers, storage, conveyance, water quality, watershed management, ecosystem restoration,  

[17:7:66,600] groundwater, and urban land use management to help meet future demands in light of uncertainties and unexpected  

[17:8:66,610] catastrophic events. This program also identifies ways for the state to: (1) help local agencies and governments prepare  

[17:9:66,620] integrated regional water management plans on a watershed basis and diversify their regional water portfolios to ensure  

[17:10:66,629] sustainable water uses, reliable water supplies, better water quality, environmental stewardship, efficient urban development,  

[17:11:66,639] protection of agriculture, and supporting a strong economy, (2) help cities, counties and local agencies prepare a Water  

[17:12:66,649] Element for their General Plans, Urban Water Management Plans and Agricultural Water Management Plans, and (3) help local  

[17:13:66,659] agencies and tribal governments improve water and land use planning coordination.  

[18:0:66,676] 3240 - IMPLEMENTATION OF THE STATE WATER RESOURCES DEVELOPMENT SYSTEM  

[19:0:66,693] The State Water Project is a water storage and delivery system that consists of 34 storage facilities (reservoirs and lakes), 21  

[19:1:66,703] pumping plants, 4 pumping-generating plants, 5 hydroelectric power plants, and over 700 miles of conveyance (canals,  

[19:2:66,713] pipelines, and tunnels). The Project provides water to over 25 million Californians and 750,000 acres of irrigated farmland.  

[20:0:66,736] * Dollars in thousands, except in Salary Range. Numbers may not add or match to other statements due to rounding of budget details.

# === PAGE 211 === [size: 612x792]
[0:0:66,13] NATURAL RESOURCES 

[1:0:408,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — RES   209 

[2:0:161,32] 3860   Department of Water Resources - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] The Department plans, designs, constructs, operates, maintains, and manages State Water Project facilities that provide water  

[3:1:66,78] to facilities located from Plumas County to Riverside County.  

[4:0:66,96] The Delta Conveyance Program is charged with improving the Delta ecosystem and ensuring water supply reliability in a safe,  

[4:1:66,105] timely, and cost-effective manner. This includes implementation of the Delta Conveyance, project specific environmental  

[4:2:66,115] commitments, and compliance with the Environmental Impact Report and Environmental Impact Statement and other state and  

[4:3:66,125] federal regulations and permits.  

[5:0:66,142] 3245 - PUBLIC SAFETY AND PREVENTION OF DAMAGE  

[6:0:66,159] This program supports the California Water Action Plan by protecting life and property from damage by floods, ensures proper  

[6:1:66,169] construction and maintenance of jurisdictional dams and levees, and provides loans for levee construction. Activities include  

[6:2:66,179] assessing the state and regional investment needs to reduce risk, preventive floodplain management to discourage unwise use  

[6:3:66,189] of areas subject to flooding, protection of floodplains, issuance of flood warnings, operation of flood control facilities,  

[6:4:66,198] coordination and supervision of flood fight activities, and annual levee and flood channel maintenance and inspection in  

[6:5:66,208] cooperation with other local, state, and federal partner agencies. This program also buys land, easements, and rights-of-way  

[6:6:66,218] for federal flood control projects and supervises the design and construction of new dams and periodic inspection and the  

[6:7:66,228] reevaluation of all existing jurisdictional dams for proper operation and maintenance. Fiscal oversight and coordination activities  

[6:8:66,238] associated with the Disaster Preparedness and Flood Prevention Bond Act of 2006 are administered under this program. The  

[6:9:66,247] program also reviews federal dam projects in coordination with federal and other state agencies with regard to dam safety.  

[7:0:66,265] 3250 - CENTRAL VALLEY FLOOD PROTECTION BOARD  

[8:0:66,284] The Central Valley Flood Protection Board has regulatory authority over the State Plan of Flood Control (SPFC) facilities,  

[8:1:66,294] designated floodways, and regulated streams in the Central Valley. The Board regulates encroachments on the system by  

[8:2:66,304] issuing permits and initiating enforcement action when necessary to maintain the integrity of the levees and floodways that  

[8:3:66,314] protect the valley's people and property. The Board manages the state's portfolio of real property held by the Sacramento-San  

[8:4:66,323] Joaquin Drainage District. The Board serves as the non-federal sponsor to the United States Army Corps of Engineers on large  

[8:5:66,333] joint state-federal levee improvement projects and assists the more than   100 local maintaining agencies that operate and  

[8:6:66,343] maintain the SPFC. The Board conducts regular public meetings, workshops and tours, providing a public forum for  

[8:7:66,353] stakeholders.  

[9:0:66,370] 3255 - SERVICES  

[10:0:66,387] This program provides technical support within the Department and expertise in the fields of water resources planning,  

[10:1:66,397] development and management; watermaster services; scientific analyses performed by DWR's chemical laboratory;  

[10:2:66,407] information technology; and mapping, surveying and engineering services for other agencies.  

[11:0:66,424] 3260 - CALIFORNIA ENERGY BOND OFFICE  

[12:0:66,441] California Energy Bond Office is responsible for managing the Electrical Power Fund and the Department of Water Resources  

[12:1:66,451] (DWR) Charge Fund. In response to the 2001 California energy crisis, for a limited period of time, the Electrical Power Charge  

[12:2:66,461] Fund purchased electric power on behalf of the state's investor-owned utilities and issued $11.3 billion in bonds. The final  

[12:3:66,471] amount of the outstanding bonds were defeased in September 2020. Bond proceeds were used to repay amounts borrowed for  

[12:4:66,480] power purchases during the 2001 energy crisis.   The DWR Charge Fund was created in 2019 by Chapter 79, Statutes of 2019  

[12:5:66,490] (AB 1054) to collect remittances from charges on investor-owned utilities ratepayers pursuant to Water Code Section 80550. 

[13:0:66,529] DETAILED EXPENDITURES BY PROGRAM  

[14:0:402,551] 2021-22* 2022-23* 2023-24*  

[14:1:115,564] PROGRAM REQUIREMENTS  

[15:0:75,576] 3230 CONTINUING FORMULATION OF THE CALIFORNIA WATER PLAN  

[15:1:115,591] State Operations:  

[16:0:75,603] 0001 General Fund $100,731 $131,413 $127,252

[2:0:161,32] 3860   Department of Water Resources - Continued 

[3:0:66,68] The Department of Water Resources has two major infrastructure programs: the State Water Project and the flood control  

[3:1:66,78] system in the Central Valley. The State Water Project is a water storage and delivery system that consists of 34 storage  

[3:2:66,88] facilities, reservoirs, and lakes, 21 pumping plants, 4 pumping-generating plants, 5 hydroelectric power plants, and over 700  

[3:3:66,98] miles of canals, pipelines, and tunnels. The Project provides water to 25 million Californians and 750,000 acres of irrigated  

[3:4:66,108] farmland. The Project also provides recreational opportunities to approximately 6 million visitors annually at 15 separate  

[3:5:66,117] reservoir-based facilities as well as public fishing access to much of the Aqueduct. Existing flood control infrastructure in the  

[3:6:66,127] Central Valley consists of 1,595 miles of levees, 348,000 acres of channels and floodways, over 800,000 linear feet of bank  

[3:7:66,137] protection, over 60 mitigation and environmental restoration sites, and 55 various flood control structures including dams, weirs,  

[3:8:66,147] pumping plants, diversion structures, gate structures, and drop structures. In general, these facilities provide more flood  

[3:9:66,156] protection in urbanized areas and less in agricultural areas.

[5:0:159,324] 3875   Sacramento-San Joaquin Delta Conservancy  

[6:0:66,345] The mission of the Sacramento-San Joaquin Delta Conservancy is to act as the primary state agency to implement ecosystem  

[6:1:66,355] restoration in the Delta and   support efforts that advance both environmental protection and the economic well-being of Delta  

[6:2:66,365] residents in a complementary manner. The Conservancy's activities include protecting and enhancing habitat and habitat  

[6:3:66,374] restoration; protecting and preserving Delta agriculture and working landscapes; providing increased opportunities for tourism  

[6:4:66,384] and recreation; promoting Delta legacy communities and economic vitality in the Delta; increasing the resilience of the Delta to  

[6:5:66,394] the effects of climate change and natural disasters such as floods and earthquakes; protecting and improving water quality;  

[6:6:66,404] assisting the Delta regional economy;   conducting activities to protect, conserve, and restore the region's physical, agricultural,  

[6:7:66,413] cultural, historical, and living resources; assisting local entities in the implementation of their habitat conservation plans and  

[6:8:66,423] natural community conservation plans; facilitating protection and safe harbor agreements under the federal Endangered  

[6:9:66,433] Species Act of 1973 and the California Endangered Species Act for adjacent land owners and local public agencies; and  

[6:10:66,443] promoting environmental education.

[0:0:66,13] 2023-24 STATE BUDGET — RES   228   NATURAL RESOURCES 

[1:0:211,69] 3885   Delta Stewardship Council  

[2:0:66,90] Established in 2009 by the Delta Reform Act, the mission of the Delta Stewardship Council, through a seven-member board, is  

[2:1:66,100] to further the state's coequal goals of providing a more reliable water supply for California and protecting, restoring, and  

[2:2:66,109] enhancing the Sacramento-San Joaquin Delta ecosystem. The goals are to be achieved in a manner that protects and  

[3:0:66,119] enhances the unique cultural, recreational, natural resource, and agricultural values of the Delta. In 2013, the Council adopted  

[3:1:66,129] a legally enforceable Delta Plan to further the coequal goals and guide state and local agency activities related to the Delta.  

[3:2:66,139] Under state law, agencies are required to coordinate their actions pursuant to the Delta Plan with the Council and the other  

[3:3:66,148] relevant agencies.   The Council is informed by scientific input from the Delta Science Program and the Delta Independent  

[3:4:66,158] Science Board. The mission of the Delta Science Program is to provide the best possible unbiased scientific information to  

[3:5:66,168] inform water and environmental decisionmaking in the Delta.
